et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	and the first treatment is good that it is cutting,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that one should not cut without a great necessity.
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and that's the instruments for cutting:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	so cut inside the curvature and do not cut too far, and see then the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine protrudes further,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	so put it back according to its natural form in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	if you have the power, because this is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	so it is necessary that you make the patient lie on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it is in the part below the belly,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	so place the head and chest higher than the parts below.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	and also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	so make sure that the injured part is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	and thus it is necessary to arrange what I say about large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	For small wounds, do as seems proper to you,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	and then take in your hands one miserable minister who holds all the rupture in his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	and that is the common manner of stitching,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it is that you take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the width of the wound.
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then leave from the head of the wound a good two fingerbreadths, and insert a needle where there is a good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce the two cheeks of the skin with the two points of the siphac.
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is below the skin inside, as long as you make it pierce from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and bring together the two heads of the siphac and tie them in three.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then strain it with a double thread around the needle from both sides,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and bring together the two cheeks of the wound harmoniously,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	and then leave another good two fingerbreadths, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then tie the thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and do not cease to do this according to how many needles you need.
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until all the wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	and are the needles medium-sized, between fine and coarse.
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	because fine needles cut through all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	therefore it is necessary that they be medium-sized.
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it is not good to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	lest they cut and open the wound before the suturing.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then cut the cheeks of the needles so that they do not disturb the patient during sleep,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and put tents or cloths on the cheeks of the needles to hold them in place.
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave them until the wound is sewn up;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	and this manner of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because one needle or two can suffice.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second stitching is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	and it is that you bring together the two thongs of leather and the two thongs of silk together with a needle, where there is one strong middle thread;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	and when you have pierced all these thongs three together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then pull the needle through to the part where you started, in the manner that one sews cloth;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and put a space of about the thickness of a lesser digit between each stitching;
ceste costure sevent li home,	this stitching is for men,
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	and I stitched a wound that a man had in his belly,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who was wounded by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was more than a palm's breadth wide,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and his intestines were torn two palms' breadth wide,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	and the wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back his intestines and it had been 24 hours since they had stopped,
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	and the wound was healed just in 15 days, and I cured him, and he was well.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And the physician had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in one place where you could not find any, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and I applied cotton twice a day on the wound, and washed it with honey water until he was well.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	take the needle and wet it on one side from the outside to the inside;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	when it has pierced the thread directly in line, then bring the end of the silk or costeau to where you have inserted the needle;
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from the other side from the inside to the outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and the understanding of this stitching is that you sew as the pelterers make the furs,
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and that you leave once the silk on one side and then take it up on the other, until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second manner of stitching, which Galen calls properly,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	is like what some people do, who bring together the two parts naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	and apply one end of the silk to the other end, in this manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	insert a needle near the end of the thread and make it pierce only that one;
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave the two ends of the silk;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outside to the inside;
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and leave both ends of the silk;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then make it pierce one and the other from the outside to the inside, in two other threads of silk that are on the other side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	and this is the second manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galien says that this phrase, and some witness it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	one must sew the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	and one should insert one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew corsets;
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and knows that when the rupture is inside the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	it is the stitching more difficult than for other places in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, and the iron has changed its color,
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	then put back the intestine and the bowels; then place on top of it the powder mixed with charcoal,
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if the iron has changed its color, then put on some ointment that is present until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and tie up the thread, and make sure the silk and thread are sewn together;
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then cure the wound as you would with others, until it is well.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	and if you don't have medicine, then apply some cotton cloth,
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it two times a day until he is well.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	Because you don't need any other medicine for most wound conditions when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will cause community with the principal members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	then it is necessary that you anoint the linen lightly with oil of temperate heat or with rose oil,
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	and place it around the wounds and under the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if he feels pain or burning in his bowels, and this often happens,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	then cleanse him with black wine, and especially if the burning comes just to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	and pierce inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine called "jun" cannot heal when it is wounded,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	and it's because of the thickness of the veins that are there, and because of the subtlety of all the body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the intestine bursts from the wound, then put it back in place as the intestines are, while it is still fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	and if it is old and has become yellow or black, then it is necessary that you bind the place that is black, lest blood should come from there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then sew what is between the ligament,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and leave the two ends hanging from the part below the wound until the intestine is extracted, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestine is rent, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	then it can be restored in some men,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	because I saw that one man was wounded in the belly with a spear;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	and the wound was on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	and it became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and there was emission and flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not stop subtletizing until he was well, and the wound was closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw him heal, I doubted that the patient might have pain in his belly;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	and there was no more harm, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	and certain experimenters say that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take fresh herbs from great roots, then bind the lips of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the herbs have opened the mouth, put it on the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	so that it stretches its mouth open;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then bind the head with a strap, and this stays so that he cannot undo it,
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then put another herb after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely covered;
et cout la plaie.	and cover the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	This treatment if done in the intestine and does not cause harm to the patient,
et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste,	and one can bind the intestine with a thin thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal,
en teil maniere:	in this manner:
pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez,	take the end of this intestinal thread that is very frayed,
et puis lie au chief de cest fil .i. fil de lin subtil tort,	and then tie to the end of this thread a thin twisted flax thread,
puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure;	then insert the thread into the needle, and sew up the intestine, and tie it off in a knot;
et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance;	and this way of sewing with herbs is not far from the path of faith and hope;
et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	and if the wound is great and wide, even when it is in one of the intestinal grooves, then there is no remedy or health, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule»,	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes swollen, is universally called a "fistula",
et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	and even when it is hollowed out and runs downward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor,	And a fistula is according to the natural concretion of hard and white flesh, or one that does not cause pain.
et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil;	and it is also hollowed out like the feathers of a bird;
et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse;	and sometimes it runs clear down below, and at other times it is thick.
aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez;	sometimes little, and at other times enough;
et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char,	and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed and has no scar,
ce n’est fuers que par une des .viiij. causes:	is not far from one of the eight causes:
c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors;	namely, by the smallness of the blood or flesh;
ou por sa malice;	or because of its wickedness;
ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char;	or because there is hard scar tissue inside and on the lips that does not allow new flesh to form;
ou il i a trop de bowe;	or because there is too much fluid;
ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit;	or the pus is rotten and the matter is of bad quality;
ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure;	or the medicine is not good in the treatment;
ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence;	or because the corruption is a manner of plague;
ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature;	or because the property in the region is slow to digest and slow to heal, and flows by natural tendency;
ou il i a voinnes ou os:	or because of veins or bones:
et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the remedies in medicine, in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And it is necessary that I inform you of the treatment for a fistula which is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors;	Know that a fistula can occur in all members of the body;
car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners,	for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves,
ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes,	or to the sacrum, or intestine, or bladder, or to any of the ribs,
ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez;	or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet;
et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	and if it is located at that which comes from the property of the principal member and similar parts.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance;	And all fistulas that are in this manner are of grievous healing, and there is nothing except labor and ignorance;
et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure,	and if there is any fistula that does not come to the point that I have said, and you have faith in the treatment,
et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier;	and if you see it well, take a tent of iron or bronze, if the fistula is straight, and then pierce;
et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc,	and if the fistula is crooked, then search for a subtle tent of lead.
car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit;	for lead bends and adapts to the curvature;
et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes,	and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot well search it with tents,
si la clisterize par l’un des pertus,	so that you can catheterize it through one of the holes,
car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie;	for the moisture so flows from one hole to another, and purifies it;
puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont,	then pierce the wound as best you can, which you know whether there is bone or nerve, and it is hollowed out by design;
et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent;	and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press your hand on him, and where he feels it;
et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine,	and when you know truly the place where it is, and whether it is away from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein,
ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit,	or in any of the places that I have told you, then bind it according to what I have told you,
et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens;	and cut away the bad flesh and corrupted scars that are inside;
et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee,	and then treat it until it is healed,
et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues,	and if the fistula is well hollowed out in its right place, then it is necessary that you bind it tightly, as much as you can,
puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule,	then I put moist tents of medicine in aqua, and tie them just to the top of the fistula,
tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons;	until the medicine consumes the superfluity that remains at the bottom;
et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then I put ointments of fresh flesh, as much as is needed, until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit,	and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said,
et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit;	If veins or nerves do not grieve or harm the principal members, as we have said;
et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee,	and if the bone is uncovered and there is corruption and blackness, then remove it all until the corruption is gone.
puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it with things of fresh flesh until it is healed.
et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant,	and if it is not healed and runs downward as before,
saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font:	know that you are not yet at the end.
si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons,	so uncover and pierce until you reach the bottom,
et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu;	and cut away all the corruption, then restore the place;
et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	and if it is thus healed, that's good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir;	If not, know that the corruption is too deep within, and you cannot come to it.
si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature;	so there is no other remedy except through the natural course of things;
et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles,	and if there is a small piece of bone corrupted and you can extract it with pincers,
si l’estrai a .i. estrument covenauble a ceu,	If one stretches it to one suitable instrument for this purpose,
et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un;	and if there are many of them, stretch all the others too, and do not leave even one;
et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour,	and if moisture makes you unwilling, and there is no error or fear,
si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	so cut and dry and flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture,	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place on the wound something that will prevent putrefaction,
et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os,	and leave it so that the flesh is putrid around the bones,
et adonc si avront plus legierement les os;	and then the bones will come out more easily;
et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse,	and if it is a large bone, such as one from the leg or hip,
si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee,	so remove only the corruption until all the marrow is gone,
puis restoure la plaie;	then restore the wound;
et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os;	and if there is great part of the corrupt flesh, and it comes just to the bone;
si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez;	so scrape and cut all the way to the corruption, and then cure it until it is sound.
et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint .i. home en sa jambe,	and I will tell you about a fistula that occurred in one man's leg,
si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	so that you may take example and aid in your work.
Il fut .i. jovencelz entor .xxx. ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors,	He was a young man of about thirty years old, who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body,
tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir;	until the matters came to the leg and it was swollen with a great abscess, and there was no reason to delay opening;
mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri,	but the doctors because of their foolishness opened too much so that the abscess burst open,
et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors;	and there came out a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and many pus-filled sores developed that all went with foul discharge from the body;
et maint mire i mirent cure entor .ij. ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains,	and many doctors tried to cure it for two years, and there was no remedy in the art of medicine,
tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit,	so that I was summoned, and I saw his leg and the medicines by which it was being treated,
et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors;	and what flowed from the sores with great abundance;
et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	and the flesh of the young man became red and had a citron-colored hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus,	I inserted a probe into one of those sores, and then searched all the sores,
et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	and I found that some came together in the middle of the leg from all parts.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os,	I hastened then, and cut into one of the sores until I uncovered a part of the bone,
et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	and I found it corrupt and perforated, and the corruption came right to the bone inside.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I removed what appeared to be corrupt from the bone, and thought that there was no other corruption except for what I had taken out;
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines over a long time, but it would not heal.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant,	and then I repeated, and discovered the bone as before,
et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and I found the corruption continued in the bone, and I removed it, and then took it out, and was anxious to set the place right.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole,	but I could not do so until I cut around a palm's length of the bone, and brought it to its full depth.
puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment,	then I restored it with medicines; and it was healed and sound quickly,
et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir,	and there was no need to continue the work except for the patient's weakness, which could not bear.
et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement,	For by the evacuation it often bled, but he was completely healed,
et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	and instead of the bone, a hard flesh grew, and he was of good disposition and had no harm or contrary from top to bottom, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, then it should be scraped in this manner:
pren .i. liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert,	take one linen cloth and strain it to the top of the open bone,
et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	and command someone to stretch it upwards;
et met .i. autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os,	and place another linen cloth, larger than the first one, and tie it over the flesh that is below the bone,
et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz,	and stretch the top so that you remove the corrupt flesh below.
et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	and uncover the flesh on the place where you see it needs to be scraped, so that the scraping does not harm the flesh.
et met .i. tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	and place a hot iron or a heated table under the bone to remove the corrupt flesh;
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and it is necessary to scrape until you can see and feel the corruption, and then scrape again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie,	And if the bone is corrupt and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part,
si descuevre la char toute; puis met .i. tison desoz,	so uncover all the flesh; then place a hot iron underneath,
et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption .i. poc, si com nos avons dit;	and then scrape from one part to the other the corruption, and be careful not to cut too deep into the corruption, just as we have said;
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupt joint, and scrape the bone on the other side where it contains;
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des .ij. jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other remedy than to cut out;
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose,	and if the corruption is in the finger of the hand or in the toe of the foot, then it is very strong,
mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	but nonetheless you must ask about this corrosion, how it appears;
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve hinder you;
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous,	and know that the incisors and scrapers for cutting these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and their appearance.
et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	and their thickness and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness;
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	and for that reason it is necessary to prepare each instrument according to the appearance of the work.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art,	and know that the work will show you the instrument you will need, according to the knowledge of this art.
et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	and the testimony of the ways of diseases;
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	so think about the instrument you need according to what is necessary.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head of the shoulder can become dislocated either due to a cause within or due to a cause outside;
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie,	and when you have medicated that corruption with medicinal treatment, and it does not benefit.
si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient,	so you must cut off that limb to the point where the corruption comes;
si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	so that the patient may escape either by death or by the greater malice of the defect of the member;
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu,	and the signs are such that the members become black, as if they had been burned by fire.
et porrist aprés la noiror, puis va celle corrosions de membre em membre,	and afterwards it puts forth after the darkness, then goes on to corrode member by member.
et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper,	and takes throughout the body; if you hasten to cover.
et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans,	and if this is due to the blow of some venomous beasts, such as sea scorpions and vipers and similar ones.
se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	if the corrosion is at the head of the joint, if it copes, and does not give space for it to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes up to the hand, then copes at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors,	and if it comes to the arm, then copes at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it's deadly.
et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and there is no remedy against death except the quantity of his virtue.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	and so it happens when the corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then copes at the other joint.
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	and if it comes to the foot, then copes all the foot.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if it goes up the leg, then copes at the knee joint.
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	and if it comes above the knee, then there is no other remedy than to let the patient die by exhaustion.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz,	and the manner of coping or sewing the member is that you bind it above and below.
et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont,	and stretch one minister's bond downward, and another minister's bond upward.
et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les .ij. liiens a .i. spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	and you loosen the flesh that is between the two bonds to one spatula wide, until the bone is uncovered.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part .i. drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain,	then you cope or sew, and put one linen wrap on each side, so that the seam does not touch the sound flesh.
et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	and another wound and abscess follows for the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment,	And if blood flows out while you are working, then cauterize the place hastily.
ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie,	or you put on some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed.
puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and care for it until it is healed.
et je te conterai k’il avint a .i. home en som piet:	and I will tell you what happened to one man in such pain:
il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu,	he had a darkness that seemed like burning fire,
et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet;	and that corrosion came first to his knee of the foot, until it corrupted all the foot.
et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez;	and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to wrap the foot, and was healed.
et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi,	and long afterwards the corrosion returned to his wrist of the hand, and he came to me.
et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions;	and I put on him things that cause a reaction after the purging of the body, and he could not stop the corrosion.
et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere;	and he said that I should cut off his hand, but I did not want to, because I had hope of causing the matter to recur.
et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist,	and I also doubted whether if I cut off his hand, he would not die.
car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre,	for the virtues of the man were weak; and he lost all hope and returned to his land.
et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez;	and he hastened to wrap his hand, and was healed.
et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	and I have not told this story except for the reason that one may need it to do another deed.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	At no time does an abscess form in a well-nourished body, and stays so long that it causes a great gathering of pus.
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	and then bursts and perforates, and the pus jumps out, and the body remains empty, just like a vessel.
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com .i. drapelz deliiez,	and the skin that is above is as subtle as one delicate veil.
et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain»,	and do not go all the way to the bone, nor all the way to the nerve, and such a disease is called "sain".
et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	and it is not called "fistula".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it comes right to the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula".
et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz;	and the skin is like this: you cut off all around that skin, and similarly when it is subtle, just like a veil.
et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	and does not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont,	And if you have faith that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not in depth.
et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	and the skin is full of flesh, so wash it with a cleansing agent thus:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor,	look to see if the abscess is large, and the pus that flows from it has a foul smell.
adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	then wash with Egyptian medicine made thus:
prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en .i. vassel au feu,	take equal parts of aloe, oil, and litharge, and mix them together in one vessel over the fire.
tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel;	until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey;
et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel,	and then take of this according to your need, and mix it with water and honey.
et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus;	and wash the abscess, and stop the fistula;
et laisse la medicine ens par .ij. houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant;	and leave the medicine in for two hours, then draw it off while sweating.
fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor;	do this many times, until the abscess is opened and the pus is removed;
et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres,	and at no time is washed with ash water.
quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus,	when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes of vine wood, and pour water over them.
puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	then let it flow, and wash with it, until you know the abscess is well opened.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres,	and if the patient cannot endure it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the ash water;
si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	then wash with water and honey or add a small amount of litharge to it.
ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver,	or wash with honey and sweet wine, for the honey has the property of purifying and cleansing.
et li vins fait aerdre le sain;	and the wine makes the skin healthy.
et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez,	and when you have done this, and you have faith that the abscess is well purged,
si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li,	then wash with that which causes flesh to grow in it.
et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin;	and it is that you take defined plaster, and mix it with rose oil and wine.
ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens;	or wash with some medicines and ointments, of which I have spoken the properties or treatment of ointments.
et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer,	and if the opening of the abscess is small, and the catheter of the syringe cannot enter it.
si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein,	so enlarge it slightly with a piece of iron, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment.
ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	or balsam ointment, until it is enlarged.
et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement .i. leu ou li clistere puisse entrer,	and if the wound is too wide, so close it and leave just enough room for one layer or the catheter to enter.
et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	and if the abscess that flows pus is above, so cut it or make it lower than where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	Since
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	For if you cannot cover the breast below as you see it,
si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est,	so arrange it in such a way that the bowstring runs to its lowest point as is.
car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char	For when the bow is deep, do not let it release its hair.
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues,	and if you cannot cover the breast below as you see,
si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe;	so arrange it in such a way that the bow runs slightly downward and does not release anything from the bow.
et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sein,	and take consolidative medicines to put on the breast,
et estent sus .i. drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sein;	and bind it with one linen cloth that covers the entire breast;
puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein .i. poc plus large dou premier,	then cover the strong place on the breast of the nipple about a poignard longer than the first one,
pues estent oignement souef sus .i. autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus,	then anoint it gently with another cloth according to the size of the nipple,
et le met sus le pertus dou sein por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois;	and place it on the breast of the nipple to lighten the bow, and do not remove the great cloth except after a few days once.
et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe,	and that which is on the breast of the nipple, removes often to remove the bow,
et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste;	and know what comes from the bow, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested;
et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non,	and take heed if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not,
et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sein,	and when your medicine has been extended in such a way that you see the nature that bursts forth on the breast of the nipple,
si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez;	so know that the breasts are already healed and approaching health;
et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie,	and then loosen it in the morning or the third day, and when you loosen the wound,
si chainge .i. autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	so change another cloth and renew the anointing.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breasts emit undigested bowels after many days, know that the breasts are not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit,	And if subtle poisons continue for a long time, do not despair of health.
car li santez aproche. Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire;	for health is approaching. For there are men who slowly let the flesh heal in their wounds, and those who do the opposite;
et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie;	and if undigested bowels burst forth from the breast after many days, know that the breasts are not healed;
et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut,	and if the breasts are slow to heal and are distended, then add medicines that are moist in substance and dry in virtue,
si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine;	as defined by anointing, for it contains a great part of vinegar, and this is the final medicine;
pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance;	take defined anointing, and mix it with rose oil, and rise from equal-portioned old wine in substance;
puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez,	then cook it and use it; and this same thing makes cooked honey increased,
quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens,	when defined anointing is not present,
ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu;	or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind it, and powder it on the honey when it is over the fire;
et puis en glue .i. drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe,	and then glue it onto a cloth, and place it on the breast, and never administer it after an aristologist's long time,
et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire;	and roots of lily celestial, which is also like flour of vetches and centaury;
et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use;	and use it in simples or compounds: grind them, and make a powder, and put it on the honey that I have said, and use it;
et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure,	and if the wound is prolonged, and is not healed by this treatment,
adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens;	then know that corruption has gone deep, and makes an impression on the bone, or hardens the members, or forms ligaments;
si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	so apply the treatment of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the apostema of the armpit
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main,	Pannicula is an apostema that arises under the armpit of the arm-pit of the hand,
ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois;	or of the foot, or by chance arises in other places;
et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient .i. aposteme chaus,	and when it is ignored and one does not take care, then a foul apostema comes forth,
et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute;	and runs and discharges bowels until it reaches the root of the armpit, and by chance may run all the way.
et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	and comes to corrosion right up to the bone, so that it brings a stinking pain, and is the joints of the toe wide, and is the color flush.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie,	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all,
si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle,	so it is necessary that you cut off all the superfluity that remains of the armpit,
puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne;	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound and the armpit is healthy;
et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece,	and if the armpit approaches the flesh inside, and begins to prick and break,
si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char,	so it is necessary that you put a cloth under the armpit that pricks the flesh,
et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement,	and tie it at the top, and cut off that subtle and delicate flesh,
et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	and put on the remaining flesh medicines that are burning and corrosive to remove all.
puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	then treat it with anointing until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner;	And if the corruption is in the bone, then cut it off and take away, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal;
et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en .i. des nous si com il est devant dit,	and if you see the toe corrupting, then cut it off in one piece just as it is said before.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat it until it is healed;
et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier;	and if it is inflamed, and bound up, and it feels great pain, then it is necessary that you heal it first;
puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus,	then cut the armpit of the scapula in a diagonal direction above.
et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor;	and take care that the cut does not come down to the flesh beneath the armpit, for the patient would feel too great pain;
et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	and if it happens, then put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of the deafness in the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus,	The toes that arise on some men's hands by chance are all fleshy.
et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle,	and by chance there is one where it has bones, and sometimes there is an armpit,
et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	and none of them are born in the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of the toes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet,	That which arises in any toe of the foot does not move.
et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	and that which arises at the joint of the toe, by chance moves;
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	the cutting of one who is fleshy is light, in such a way:
taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	cut it at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	That which arises at the root of the joint is difficult to cure: it's better to leave it as is.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os,	In one who is born or will be at the end of nine months, it is necessary that you cauterize the skin first around just to the bone.
puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	then cauterize the bone with a suitable silk thread for this, then care for it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wounds that come from having to assemble come by birth, or by sudden wound, or by burning with fire, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz;	It is necessary that you cauterize that wound, so that it may be repaired according to its natural forms;
puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent;	then put between two tents or wet cloths soaked in rose oil, so that they do not stick together;
ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	or you put between two thin pieces of plank, until the flesh is sewn, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a wound comes to any of its two with the palm, then cauterize that wound as it is necessary.
Des vils	Note: This appears to be the start of a new section or paragraph, rather than a complete sentence.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Veins are great swollen vessels full of melancholic superfluities that come to many members of the body;
et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	and more commonly occur in the legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is necessary therefore that you administer to him sometimes purging of gall, and then heal the wound with basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc .ij. manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir;	The iron cure is according to two manners: one is by cauterizing and then drawing out the black blood;
et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	and the other manner is that you open the wound and draw it out entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez,	The incision is according to this manner: first, arise the leg with hot water very strongly, until the thick blood is thinned.
puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	then restrain the leg of the patient from above the knee to the part below the kneecap;
puis cope la voinne en .i. leu, ou en .ij. ou en .iij., d’une taille large,	then cauterize the wound in one place, or two places, or three places, with a broad incision,
puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir;	then lift and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the patient's virtues can endure.
et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire;	and then tie it up, and command that he eat meat causing black gall.
et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	and begin the evacuation and healing again when the wounds are full and bad for the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil,	The healing of it is according to this manner: rise the leg of the patient, if there are many hairs.
puis le met ou bain, et li. arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes;	then put it in a bath, and arise the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and swell the wounds;
et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville;	and if you do not have a bath, then heat it by the fire, and then cauterize the place near the wound from the top of the kneecap to the part below the ankle;
puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent;	then apply the skin to its original place, and scrape off the wound from each part, until it appears when you feel;
et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche;	and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems also like a white cord;
puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier,	then bind the strip below, until it is lifted from the skin, and then tie it to its original place lightly;
puis le cope en .i. autre leu ensus iij. dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere,	then cauterize in one other place, above three fingers; then scrape off the skin over the wound until it appears.
puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers;	then lift it to its place, just as you did, and tie it to another skin, just as you did first.
puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet,	then make another incision, or more if you need them, then lift it, and cauterize at the heel of the foot.
puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope;	then draw it out and lift to the second incision; then pull it from incision to incision, until it comes out entirely, then cauterize.
et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil fort double,	and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, then put an awl into each strong doubled thread;
et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz .i. rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse;	and tie and draw it out, and put below one strip, and turn your hand from side to side, until it comes out.
et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide;	and beware that it does not cauterize, for if it does, then one cannot draw it out or lift it, and it comes to harm the patient.
et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	and when you have drawn it all out, then put a wet wool cloth soaked in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound, and care for it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit,	And if the vein is contracted and twisted and swollen together, and it is not straight, as we have said,
si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	then it is necessary that you cut it awry, but do not cauterize it; and draw it out as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne;	The shape of the iron with which one cauterizes the vein is curved, and does not cut off, so that it may cauterize the wound.
et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	and is of great curvature, for if it were thin, it would cut off the vein, but be thick as we have said, and this is the shape:
De la voinne civile	Note: This appears to be the start of a new section or paragraph, rather than a complete sentence.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This wound is located in the legs, in hot and dry places where there are no herbs or trees, and on land where there is no moisture.
et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir,	and by chance it may occur in another part than the legs, and this happens because of the corruption that comes from below the skin.
si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	as if a serpent or worm were to come forth inside the body, and then be enclosed between the skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation,	And if the signs of the beginning of this wound are that it comes in the leg with a very great inflammation,
puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	then the swelling changes color and the wound begins to emerge forth like a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a .ij. З., et la noe,	When the swelling opens up, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of plank from one and a half to two and a half hands' width, and tie it tightly.
et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe;	and leave the plank on the leg, and every time it seems to be getting worse, wrap it around the plank and tie it tightly.
et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue;	and if it is too long, then cut off a part of it and wrap the remaining portion around the plank, and do not cauterize its root until it has come out entirely.
car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie;	for if you cauterize it, then it will go back into the flesh, and cause an abscess and corruption at that place, and a bad disease.
por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors;	therefore it is necessary that she be treated little by little until the top, and that none remain in the body.
et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de .v. paumes de lonc, ou de .x.,	and sometimes this wound is such when it is treated with five or ten fingers' width.
et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de .x. paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute .i. rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons,	and one man came to me, whose it was, and it issued from ten fingers' width long, and when you cauterize it, then put in one strip or peg, and pierce it right down to the bottom.
si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	So that all goes well; and let the matter inside be emptied, and bring to the place medicines in sufficient quantity for some day, then care for it as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet,	And at this vein, many times apply rainwater, and similarly when it opens in the joints of the foot or foot.
et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	and it comes out much pus, and where it jumps rainwater; then care for it as we have said before.
Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This disease is called in our land "disease of oxen", because it often occurs in oxen,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes all through the body rising and descending.
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	and it can be felt as it moves from member to member, until it breaks through the skin where it goes, and jumps out.
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	and is caused by some sort of corruption of humors, such as those that come from vermin and serpents and lice and ascarids or the belly.
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	and one doubts about its malice, for when it goes through the body and mounts to the head and comes to the eye.
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	by chance it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it cured and pulled out, then one cannot prevent it from happening again unless it is taken out.
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so then it is necessary that you tie the place above and below with a strong thread tightly.
puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves,	then cut on top and pull it out, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh, and you cannot find it.
si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	then cauterize it with fire above until it dies;
et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit;	and the greatest harm that it does is that it destroys the eye, as we have said.
et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	and if you see it coming to the head near the eye, then hold a small cloth under it tightly, then cut on top and pull it out;
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	and it is necessary to use the patient with purging medicine of the body for the bad humors carried.
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	and beware of foods that promote corruption.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakkirir", and is a pain that comes to some members,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	and then moves from member to member; and I have seen this which I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm.
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	and soon after, I saw it rise also like a worm on the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	faster than anything, just like sharp silver when it cuts from one place to another;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	the pain left that place and settled in the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	and then a little later it ran all through the body, until it came to the other arm.
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	then she told me that it was running around the body again, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed how she moved like that from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in such a manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	However, I had seen many who had moved well and had their pain from one place to another,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but never had I seen it, as I saw it in the woman.
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	and I thought that it was because the woman had a dry body and her veins were uncovered,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	and therefore this windiness appeared constrained;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	and do not appear according to this reason in those who are sweet and have moist bodies and responded veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see this disease cured, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	then bind above and below quickly, and then cut on top until that constrained windiness comes out.
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your own eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	then use remedies that stop windiness, such as fetid pills and viper pills, and similar others.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they strike.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The diversity of them is that there are some with large points, and small, and barbed, and smooth.
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with fragments;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and that which strikes in some member strikes in two ways: or it enters the main principal member,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	such as brain, heart, liver, kidneys, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it strikes then in any part of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you later appears:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	so it is necessary that you beware of the extraction of this arrow, for death comes after in many conditions;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow strikes and pierces the bone, and springs out the sac that is above the brain.
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	It is when there is blindness and numbness and confusion and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of tongue, and spasm and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of bile.
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and by chance it is without force in the nostrils or ears; and by chance affects speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and bursts forth from the moist white wound resembling pustules, and springs out also like a bruise on flesh.
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if you see this sign, then hold back from curing, and pull out the arrow if it is not embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it strikes the heart is that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty.
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	and by chance the arrow becomes still like a pustule, and in it flows black blood, and comes with coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	then you should not doubt that death is present.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow when it strikes the kidneys is that without foam or bubbles it bursts forth from the wound, and the throat swells, and the patient's face turns pale, and they sigh deeply and seek cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow strikes in the cover of the breastbone, it is between the little ribs; and pours out great gall and great pain and sighs; and all the members of the shoulders are moved.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow shoots or falls on the stomach, by chance some undigested thing from the wound may jump out of the flesh.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow falls on the belly, and no fragment of the arrow passes through the intestine route, then there is no hope for a cure, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow falls in the bladder, and the urine leaps out and flows away, and the patient feels very painful: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and the neck and the throat and the shoulder and the armpit and the spine of the back and the nape and the heel and the knee and the leg and similar members, are safe according to many conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you, because of which you should act similarly.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened to one man whose arrow fell on the nose in the root of the night:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried to remove it and pulled it out from under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without numbness.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And I pulled out an arrow that had fallen in the fat of the eye under the eyebrow fold.
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	and the arrow was stuck, and I could not pull it out except for the tip towards the tree.
